Contradictory of General Temporal Propositions
Author identifies the contradictory of the general temporal proposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any general temporal proposition by applying the rules of quantity, quality, and modality flip.

Core Idea
The contradictory of 'Every A is B at time T' is 'Some A is not B at time T' with possibility.

In modal logic, contradictions of temporally restricted propositions require careful handling. The general temporal proposition asserts necessity at a specific time. Its contradictory flips quantity and quality while preserving the time and shifting modality from necessity to general possibility. This rule mirrors the standard square of opposition but with a temporal anchor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original proposition as general temporal (waqtiyya 'amma)
The proposition has a universal quantifier ('every') and a specific time condition: 'Every A is B at time T'. The modality is implicit necessity (since it is asserted as a universal temporal fact).
In Arabic: 'كل أب وقت كذا'
2
Flip quantity and quality
The contradictory must be opposite in both quantity (universal → particular) and quality (affirmative → negative). So 'Every A is B' becomes 'Some A is not B'.
3
Adjust modality to general possibility
The original asserts necessity (bi-l‑ḍarūra) at time T. Its contradictory asserts that it is possibly not the case at that same time: 'Some A is not B at time T with general possibility (bi-l‑imkān al‑ʿāmm)'.
The time condition remains unchanged.
4
Construct the contradictory proposition
Combine the results: 'Some A is not B at time T with general possibility.' This is the contradictory (naqīḍ) of the original general temporal proposition.
Formally: 'بعض أ ليس ب وقت كذا بالإمكان العام'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في الوقتية العامة فذلك هو الممكنة العامة الوقتية المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال بالضرورة كل «أب» وقت كذا، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» وقت كذا بالإمكان العام.
As for the general temporal, that is the general possible temporal that is opposite in quantity and quality, so it is said: necessarily, every A is B at such-and-such time; some A is not B at such-and-such time with general possibility.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory of a general temporal proposition (waqtiyya 'amma). This proposition specifies a particular time for the predicate: 'Every A is B at time T'. The contradictory is the general possible temporal (mumkina 'amma waqtiyya) that is opposite in quantity and quality. That is, 'Some A is not B at time T with general possibility'. The time condition remains the same in both, but the modality changes from necessity to possibility and the quantity/quality flip.

Key Terms
الوقتية العامة
الممكنة العامة الوقتية
المخالفة كما وكيفا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No A is B at time T
B) Some A is not B at time T with general possibility
C) Some A is B at time T with necessity
D) Every A is not B at time T

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a general temporal proposition is a particular negative possible temporal proposition with the same time condition.

Contradictories of the Special Temporal Proposition
Author gives two possible contradictories for the special temporal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible contradictories of a special temporal proposition and explain the logical basis for each.

Core Idea
The special temporal has two contradictories because of its non-perpetuity clause.

The special temporal proposition (al-waqtiyya al-khassa) affirms a predicate for a specific time but denies its permanence. This lesson explains how to find its contradictory, which can take two forms depending on whether you negate the temporal affirmation or the non-perpetuity clause.

Guided Path
1
Recall the structure of the special temporal
The special temporal is 'Every A is B at time T, but not perpetually'. It has two components: an affirmation limited to T and a negation of perpetuity.
2
Apply the general rule of contradiction for quantified propositions
The contradictory of a universal affirmative is a particular negative. However, because of the temporal restriction and the 'not perpetually' clause, we must consider both components.
3
Identify the first possible contradictory
The first contradictory is a general possible temporal proposition that is opposite in quantity and quality: changing 'Every A is B at T but not perpetually' to 'Some A is not B at T' (particular negative) while retaining the temporal frame.
This negates the affirmative component.
4
Identify the second possible contradictory
The second contradictory is a perpetual temporal proposition that agrees in quality: changing 'not perpetually' to 'perpetually', so the contradictory becomes 'Every A is B perpetually (at all times in that temporal frame)'. This negates the non-perpetuity component.
This keeps the quantity and quality of the original but makes it perpetual.
5
Understand why there are two options
Because the original proposition has two conditions (being B at T and not being B always), the contradictory can fully negate it by negating either condition. The two forms given are the standard contradictories recognized in logic.
Both are valid contradictories as they completely oppose the original.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الوقتية الخاصة هو الممكنة العامة الوقتية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الوقتية الموافقة كيفا.
And in the special temporal, it is the general possible temporal that is opposite in quantity and quality, or the perpetual temporal that agrees in quality.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage gives the contradictory of the special temporal proposition (waqtiyya khassa). This proposition has the form 'Every A is B at time T, but not perpetually'. The contradictory can be either a general possible temporal opposite in quantity and quality, or a perpetual temporal (da'ima waqtiyya) that agrees in quality. The pattern is similar to the special conditional: because of the extra restriction of non-perpetuity, there are two possible contradictories.

Key Terms
الوقتية الخاصة
الدائمة الوقتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The special temporal proposition has two possible contradictories because it contains both an affirmative temporal claim and a negative perpetual claim, each of which can be negated independently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the proposition 'Every human is mortal at the moment of death but not perpetually' (an example from kalam on temporality), write out its two contradictories using the forms from this lesson.
?
In a debate on whether the world is created or eternal, a mutakallim says 'The world is temporally originated but not eternal'. Identify the two possible contradictories of this statement.

Contradictory of the General Distributive Proposition
Author identifies the contradictory of the general distributive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any general distributive proposition by adjusting quantity, quality, and temporal quantifier.

Core Idea
The contradictory of 'every A is B at some time' is 'some A is never B with general possibility'.

General distributive propositions involve a temporal quantifier: they assert that the predicate holds for the subject at some unspecified time. Finding their contradictory requires careful handling of this temporal element. In this lesson, we will learn the rule given by the author: the contradictory must be opposite in quantity, quality, and modality, negating the existential temporal quantifier with 'at all'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposition type
Recognize that the original proposition is a general distributive (muntashira 'amma): 'Every A is B at some time'. Note its universal quantity, affirmative quality, and existential temporal quantifier.
2
Determine the contradictory's quantity and quality
The contradictory must be opposite in both: change universal to particular, and affirmative to negative. So the contradictory is particular negative: 'Some A is not B ...'
This follows the standard square of opposition for categorical propositions.
3
Negate the temporal quantifier
The original says 'at some time'. To deny that, we say 'at all' (aslan) meaning 'never'. So 'Some A is not B at all'.
This is necessary because the original claim is about existence at a time.
4
Add the appropriate modality
The author specifies that the contradictory uses 'general possibility' (imkan 'am). This is because it is not necessary that some A is never B; it is only possible.
The modality contrasts with the original, which may be absolute or necessary depending on context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المنتشرة العامة هو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال بالضرورة كل «أب» في وقت من الأوقات، بعض «أ» ليس ب أصلا بالإمكان العام.
And in the general distributive, it is the general possible that is opposite in quantity and quality, so it is said: necessarily, every A is B at some time; some A is not B at all with general possibility.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory of a general distributive proposition (muntashira 'amma). This proposition asserts that the predicate holds for the subject at some unspecified time: 'Every A is B at some time'. Its contradictory is the general possible proposition opposite in quantity and quality: 'Some A is never B with general possibility'. Note that the contradictory uses 'at all' (aslan) to negate the existential temporal quantifier.

Key Terms
المنتشرة العامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Some A is never B with necessity
B) Some A is not B at some time
C) Some A is not B at all with general possibility
D) No A is B at some time

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a general distributive proposition is a particular negative with general possibility, negating the temporal quantifier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Finding Contradictories for the Special Distributive
Author gives two possible contradictories for the special distributive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible contradictories of the special distributive proposition (muntashira khassa) and apply the rule to determine the correct contradictory for any special distributive in Islamic logical texts.

Core Idea
Contradictories of special modals require two forms: one opposite in quantity and quality, one agreeing in quality but changing modality.

In this passage, the author explains how to find the contradictory (naqid) of a special distributive proposition (al-muntashira al-khassa). This proposition affirms that every A is B at some time but not perpetually. The contradictory must be of two types: either a general possible proposition opposite in quantity and quality, or a perpetual absolute proposition agreeing in quality. Understanding this is crucial for constructing valid arguments and refutations in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original proposition
Recognise a special distributive proposition: it has the form 'Every A is B not perpetually but at some time'. The key is the non-perpetuity condition.
For example: 'Every created thing is temporally originated at some time but not perpetually.'
2
Recall standard contradictory patterns
Normally, a universal affirmative's contradictory is a particular negative. But here the modality (non-perpetuity) adds complexity.
The author gives two possibilities because the modality interacts with quantity and quality.
3
Apply the first option: general possible opposite
The contradictory can be a general possible proposition that is opposite in quantity (particular instead of universal) and quality (negative instead of affirmative). It says: 'Some A is not B at all with general possibility'.
This is 'some A is never B' in a possible sense.
4
Apply the second option: perpetual absolute agreeing
Alternatively, the contradictory can be a perpetual absolute that agrees in quality (affirmative) but changes the modality to permanence: 'Some A is B perpetually'. This undermines the original's non-perpetuity.
This is 'some A is always B' without any restriction.
5
Verify the contradiction
Check that the original and each option cannot both be true and cannot both be false simultaneously, satisfying the conditions of contradiction (al-tanāquḍ).
The non-perpetuity claim is negated either by denial of the predicate at all times or by assertion of it at all times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المنتشرة الخاصة هو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفًا فيقال بالضرورة كل «أب» لا دائما بل في وقت من الأوقات، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» أصلا بالإمكان العام أو بعضه «أ» دائمًا.
And in the special distributive, it is the general possible that is opposite in quantity and quality, or the perpetual absolute that agrees in quality, so it is said: necessarily, every A is B not perpetually but at some time; some A is not B at all with general possibility, or some A is B perpetually.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory of the special distributive proposition (muntashira khassa). This proposition adds non-perpetuity to the general distributive: 'Every A is B not perpetually but at some time'. The contradictory can be either a general possible opposite in quantity and quality ('some A is never B with general possibility') or a perpetual absolute that agrees in quality ('some A is B perpetually'). This follows the pattern seen with other special modalities.

Key Terms
المنتشرة الخاصة
الممكنة العامة
الدائمة الموافقة
المخالفة كما وكيفا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a possible contradictory of the special distributive proposition as described in the passage?
A) No A is B
B) Some A is not B at all with general possibility
C) Every A is B at all times
D) Some A is not B at some time

Key Takeaway
The special distributive has two contradictories: one opposite in quantity and quality (general possible particular negative), and one agreeing in quality but changing to perpetual absolute (particular affirmative).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Contradictory of Existence Non-Necessary Propositions
Author identifies the contradictory of the existence non-necessary proposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any existence non-necessary (wujudiyya la daruriyya) proposition and explain why it takes two possible forms.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a non-necessary existence proposition is either a perpetual opposite or a necessary agreement.

In this passage, the author explains how to negate a specific type of modal proposition: the existence non-necessary. Unlike simple categorical propositions, modal propositions require careful handling of both quantity and quality, and also the modality. You will learn the two possible forms the contradictory can take.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original proposition
The original is 'Every A is B not necessarily' – universal affirmative with non-necessity modality. Note the form: qadiyya wujudiyya la daruriyya.
2
Recognize the contradictory options
The author gives two options: (1) a perpetual proposition opposite in quantity (particular) and quality (negative): 'Some A is not B perpetually'; (2) a necessary proposition opposite in quantity (particular) but same in quality (affirmative): 'Some A is B necessarily'.
Both are valid because each describes a scenario where the original would be false.
3
Understand the logic behind two forms
Since the original says 'not necessarily', it leaves open two ways it could be false: if there is a perpetual lack (some A never B) or if there is a necessary presence (some A necessarily B). These cover all possibilities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في الوجودية اللا ضرورية فذلك هو الدائمة المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الضرورة الموافقة كيفًا فيقال كل «أب» لا بالضرورة، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» دائمًا أو بعضه «ب» بالضرورة.
As for the existence non-necessary, that is the perpetual that is opposite in quantity and quality, or the necessary that agrees in quality, so it is said: every A is B not necessarily; some A is not B perpetually, or some A is B necessarily.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory of an existence non-necessary proposition (wujudiyya la daruriyya). This proposition asserts actual existence without necessity: 'Every A is B but not necessarily'. The contradictory can be either a perpetual proposition that is opposite in quantity and quality ('some A is not B perpetually') or a necessary proposition that agrees in quality ('some A is B necessarily'). Here, the original is a universal affirmative with non-necessity; its contradictory can be a particular negative perpetual or a particular affirmative necessary. This concludes the discussion of necessity and non-necessity among the modal propositions.

Key Terms
الوجودية اللا ضرورية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Some A is not B perpetually
B) Some A is B necessarily
C) Every A is not B necessarily
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of an existence non-necessary proposition can be either a perpetual proposition opposite in quantity and quality or a necessary proposition opposite in quantity but same in quality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Contradictories of Conditional Propositions ('Urfiyya): General and Specific
Author defines contradictory pairs for conditional propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct contradictory proposition for any general or specific conditional ('urfiyya) based on whether the condition attaches to the subject or predicate.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a conditional removes a restriction, not the whole relation.

In this passage, the author explains how to find the contradictory of conditional propositions, which assert a relationship as long as a condition holds without necessity. The key is that the contradictory does not simply negate the entire proposition; rather, it negates one of the restrictions. Understanding this is crucial for performing immediate inferences in modal logic, as used in kalam and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type and side
Determine whether the conditional is general ('urfiyya 'amma) or specific ('urfiyya khassa), and whether the condition is attached to the subject or predicate. This determines the set of restrictions.
2
List the restrictions
General conditionals have only the condition itself (e.g., 'as long as it is A'). Specific conditionals have additional restrictions beyond the basic condition.
3
Select the contradictory form
For general conditionals, the contradictory is always a general absolute temporal proposition (المطلقة العامة الحينية) that denies the relation at the moment the condition holds. For specific conditionals, it may be either a general absolute temporal or a perpetual proposition (الدائمة), depending on which restriction is removed.
4
Express the contradictory
Write the contradictory using the pattern: for subject side: 'Some A is not B when it is A' (general absolute) or 'Some A is B perpetually' (perpetual). For predicate side: similar but with condition on the predicate.
5
Verify contradiction conditions
Check that the contradictory differs in container (time: temporary vs. perpetual) and/or modality (absolute vs. perpetual) as required by the passage.
The author states the contradictory must be 'mukhalifa kama wa kayfa' (opposite in container and modality) or 'muwafaqa kayfa' (matching in modality).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[13] وأما في العرفية العامة من جانب الموضوع فذلك وهو الذي يدل على رفع قيد من القيود هو المطلقة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» ما دام «أ» ، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» حين هو «أ» بالإطلاق العام. [14] وأما العرفية الخاصة ففيها من القيود ما ليس في العامة، والذي يدل على رفع قيد من تلك القيود هو المطلقة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» لا دائما بل ما دام «أ»، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» حين هو «أ» بالإطلاق العام أو بعضه «ب» دائما. [15] وأما في العرفية العامة من جانب المحمول فذلك أيضًا هو المطلقة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» مادام «ب»، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» حين هو «ب» بالإطلاق العام. [16] وفي العرفية الخاصة من جانب المحمول هو المطلقة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» لا دائما بل ما دام «ب»، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» حين هو «ب» بالإطلاق العام أو بعضه «ب» دائمًا. فلا تفاوت بين المشروطة والعرفية إلا في الضرورة؛ إذ الضرورة اللازمة في المشروطة غير لازمة في العرفية.
[13] As for the general conditional from the subject side, that [contradictory] is the general absolute temporal, opposite in container and modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B as long as it is A, some A is not B when it is A' with general absolute. [14] As for the specific conditional, it has restrictions not present in the general, and what indicates the removal of one of those restrictions is the general absolute temporal, opposite in container and modality, or the perpetual matching in modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B not perpetually but as long as it is A, some A is not B when it is A' with general absolute, or 'some A is B perpetually.' [15] As for the general conditional from the predicate side, that also is the general absolute temporal opposite in container and modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B as long as it is B, some A is not B when it is B' with general absolute. [16] And in the specific conditional from the predicate side, it is the general absolute temporal opposite in container and modality, or the perpetual matching in modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B not perpetually but as long as it is B, some A is not B when it is B' with general absolute, or 'some A is B perpetually.' There is no difference between the conditioned (mashruta) and the conditional ('urfiyya) except in necessity; for the necessity required in the conditioned is not required in the conditional.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage defines the contradictory propositions for conditional propositions ('urfiyya), distinguishing between general and specific types and whether the condition is attached to the subject or the predicate. The author explains that the contradictory of a general conditional from the subject side is a general absolute temporal proposition that contradicts both in container (time) and modality (how). For example, 'Every A is B as long as it is A' is contradicted by 'Some A is not B when it is A' under general absolute modality. For specific conditionals, which have additional restrictions, the contradictory may be either a general absolute temporal or a perpetual proposition matching the modality, depending on which restriction is removed. The same principles apply when the condition is on the predicate side. The passage concludes with a key clarification: the only difference between conditioned (mashruta) and conditional propositions is the presence of necessity in conditioned propositions.

Key Terms
العرفية العامة
العرفية الخاصة
المطلقة العامة الحينية
الدائمة
المشروطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the contradictory of the general conditional from the subject side 'Every A is B as long as it is A'?
A) Some A is not B when it is A (general absolute)
B) Every A is B perpetually
C) Some A is B when it is A
D) No A is B at any time

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a conditional proposition is formed by negating one of its restrictions, resulting in a proposition that differs in time or modality, not simply a negation of the whole.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Contradictories of Temporal and Spread Propositions
Author defines contradictory pairs for temporal and spread propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any given temporal or spread proposition based on its type (general/specific) and modality.

Core Idea
General temporal/spread propositions have one contradictory; specific ones have two options.

In the previous lesson, we learned the contradictories for perpetual propositions. Now we extend the analysis to temporal (waqtiyya) and spread (muntashira) propositions. The key is to distinguish whether the proposition is general or specific, and whether the time is definite (temporal) or indefinite (spread). The contradictory patterns follow consistent rules, which we will break down step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposition type
Determine if the proposition is temporal (specified definite time) or spread (unspecified time). Also classify it as general or specific based on the phrasing. For example, 'Every fasting person eats during Ramadan' is a general temporal proposition.
General temporal: holds for a definite time without necessity. Specific temporal: adds a restriction (e.g., 'only during Ramadan').
2
Apply the general rule
For a general proposition (temporal or spread), the contradictory is the general absolute opposite in container and modality. This means you deny the predicate at the exact time (or at all times if spread). For example, the contradictory of 'Every A is B during time T' is 'Some A is not B during time T'.
General absolute temporal means the negation uses the same time specification.
3
Handle specific propositions
For a specific proposition, you have two choices: either use the general absolute opposite (removing the restriction) or use a perpetual proposition that matches the modality. For example, if the original is 'Every A is B not perpetually but during T', the contradictory can be 'Some A is not B during T' (general absolute) or 'Some A is B perpetually'.
The perpetual option is available because the specific temporal proposition has a built-in exception ('not perpetually'), so the contradictory can affirm perpetuity.
4
Distinguish temporal from spread
For spread propositions, the time is unspecified. The general spread contradictory denies the predicate 'at all' (i.e., at no time). For specific spread, the same two-option rule applies: either general absolute (denying at all) or perpetual (affirming perpetually).
In spread propositions, the phrase 'as long as some time' (غير معين) is key; the negation must be absolute ('not at all').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[17] وأما في الوقتية العامة من الدائمات فذلك هو المطلقة العامة الوقتية المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» ما دام وقت كذا، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» وقت كذا بالإطلاق العام. [18] وفي الوقتية الخاصة هو المطلقة العامة الوقتية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» لا دائما بل ما دام وقت كذا، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» وقت كذا بالإطلاق العام أو بعضه «ب» دائمًا. [19] وفي المنتشرة العامة هو المطلقة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» ما دام وقت كذا؛ وذلك الوقت غير معين، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» أصلا بالإطلاق العام. [20] وفي المنتشرة الخاصة هو المطلقة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة كيفا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» لا دائما بل ما دام وقت كذا؛ وذلك الوقت غير معين أيضًا، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» أصلا بالإطلاق العام أو بعضه «ب» دائمًا.
[17] As for the general temporal among perpetuals, that is the general absolute temporal opposite in container and modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B as long as such-and-such time, some A is not B at such-and-such time' with general absolute. [18] And in the specific temporal, it is the general absolute temporal opposite in container and modality, or the perpetual matching in modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B not perpetually but as long as such-and-such time, some A is not B at such-and-such time' with general absolute, or 'some A is B perpetually.' [19] In the general spread, it is the general absolute opposite in container and modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B as long as some time, that time being unspecified, some A is not B at all' with general absolute. [20] In the specific spread, it is the general absolute opposite in container and modality, or the perpetual in modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B not perpetually but as long as some time, that time being also unspecified, some A is not B at all' with general absolute, or 'some A is B perpetually.'
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage continues the enumeration of contradictory pairs, now for temporal (waqtiyya) and spread (muntashira) propositions. Temporal propositions specify a definite time, while spread propositions involve an unspecified time. For general temporal propositions (e.g., 'Every A is B during a specified time'), the contradictory is a general absolute temporal proposition that denies the predicate at that time. For specific temporal propositions, which have additional restrictions, the contradictory can be either a general absolute temporal (removing the restriction) or a perpetual proposition (matching the modality). Similarly, for general spread propositions (with an unspecified time), the contradictory is a general absolute that denies the predicate at all times. For specific spread propositions, the contradictory is either general absolute or perpetual. The pattern is consistent: general types take a single contradictory (general absolute temporal), while specific types have two options (general absolute or perpetual matching in modality).

Key Terms
الوقتية العامة
الوقتية الخاصة
المنتشرة العامة
المنتشرة الخاصة

B) Every A is B perpetually
C) Some A is B during Ramadan
D) No A is B at any time

Key Takeaway
General temporal/spread propositions have exactly one contradictory (general absolute opposite), while specific temporal/spread propositions have two possible contradictories: general absolute opposite or perpetual matching in modality.

Contradictories of Modal Propositions
Defining contradictory rules for modal propositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any existential non-perpetual, specific possible, more specific possible, or future possibility proposition using the rules of modality and container.

Core Idea
Every modal proposition has a contradictory defined by opposite or matching in container and modality; contradiction is always reciprocal.

In this passage, the author explains how to find the contradictory pairs for four types of modal propositions: existential non-perpetual, specific possible, more specific possible, and future possibility. The key is to consider both the container (e.g., perpetual, necessary) and the modality (e.g., existence, necessity). Understanding these rules is crucial for constructing valid arguments in Islamic theology and jurisprudence, where modal statements about obligations, possibilities, and impossibilities are common.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposition type
Determine whether the proposition is existential non-perpetual (وجودية لا دائمة), specific possible (ممكنة خاصة), more specific possible (أخص), or future possibility (إمكان استقبالي). This tells you which category of contradictory rule to apply.
The passage groups these as distinct cases.
2
Determine the container and modality of the contradictory
For each type, the contradictory can be either the opposite in both container and modality (مخالفة كما وكيفا) or the same container with opposite modality (موافقة كيفا). For existential non-perpetual, the container is perpetual; for the specific possible, it is necessary.
The passage gives two forms: e.g., for existential non-perpetual: 'some A is not B perpetually' (opposite) or 'some A is B perpetually' (same container, opposite quantity).
3
Apply the rule with quantity and quality
The contradictory must differ in both quantity (universal/particular) and quality (affirmative/negative) as per standard contradictory rules, but the modal adjustments are as above. For example, the contradictory of 'every A is B with specific possibility' (universal affirmative) is 'some A is not B with necessity' (particular negative) or 'some A is B with necessity' (particular affirmative) depending on the chosen form.
The passage emphasizes that the specific possible may be necessary in cases like temporal propositions, so necessity here covers both necessity of existence (obligation) and necessity of non-existence (impossibility).
4
Verify reciprocity
Check that the relation is symmetric: if proposition P contradicts Q, then Q also contradicts P. The author states this explicitly for the absolute/perpetual and general possible/necessary pairs.
This principle ensures no one-sided contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[21] وأما في الوجودية اللا دائمة فهو الدائمة المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفًا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» لا دائما ، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» دائمًا أو بعضه «ب» دائمًا. [22] وأما في الممكنة الخاصة فهو الضرورية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الضرورية الموافقة كيفًا فيقال كل «أ» «ب» بالإمكان الخاص بعض «أ» ليس «ب» بالضرورة أو بعضه «ب» بالضرورة والضرورة فيه إما ضرورة العدم وهي الامتناع، وإما ضرورة الوجود وهي الوجوب في الحقيقة وإلا لا يصح، فإن الممكنة الخاصة قد تكون ضرورية نحو الوقتية والمنتشرة وأمثالهما. [23] وأما في الأخص فكذلك لكن الضرورة فيها بوجه من الوجوه فيقال كل «أ» «ب» بالإمكان الأخص، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» بالضرورة أي ضرورة كانت أو بعضه «ب» بالضرورة كذلك. [24] وعلى هذا في الإمكان الاستقبالي، فاعتبر بما عرفت فإن اعتبار الجهة في التناقض لا يختلف باختلاف القضايا الموجبة والسالبة والكلية والجزئية، والقضية لا تناقض قضية أخرى إلا وأن تكون تلك القضية تناقضها، فالمطلقة تناقض الدائمة فالدائمة إذن تناقض المطلقة. وكذا الممكنة العامة تناقض الضرورية، فالضرورية إذن تناقضها؛ إذ المنافاة بين القضيتين لا تكون مخصوصة بأحد الجانبين، وهذا ظاهر.
[21] As for the existential non-perpetual, it is the perpetual opposite in container and modality, or the perpetual matching in modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B not perpetually, some A is not B perpetually' or 'some A is B perpetually.' [22] As for the specific possible, it is the necessary opposite in container and modality, or the necessary matching in modality, so it is said: 'Every A is B with specific possibility, some A is not B with necessity' or 'some A is B with necessity.' And necessity here is either necessity of non-existence, which is impossibility, or necessity of existence, which is obligation in reality, otherwise it is invalid; for the specific possible may be necessary, like temporal and spread and their likes. [23] As for the more specific, it is similar but necessity is in some respect, so it is said: 'Every A is B with more specific possibility, some A is not B with necessity' i.e., whatever necessity, or 'some A is B with necessity' likewise. [24] And similarly for future possibility. Consider what you have learned, for the consideration of modality in contradiction does not differ between affirmative and negative, universal and particular propositions. A proposition only contradicts another if that proposition is its contradictory. Thus the absolute contradicts the perpetual, and so the perpetual also contradicts the absolute. Likewise, the general possible contradicts the necessary, and so the necessary also contradicts it. For the opposition between two propositions is not confined to one side, and this is clear.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage covers the contradictory pairs for existential non-perpetual, specific possible (mumkin khāṣṣ), more specific possible (akhaṣṣ), and future possibility (imkān istiqbālī). For existential non-perpetual propositions (e.g., 'Some A is B but not always'), the contradictory can be a perpetual proposition either opposite or matching in modality. For specific possible propositions, the contradictory involves necessity: either necessary opposite or necessary matching. The author clarifies that necessity here can be either necessity of non-existence (impossibility) or necessity of existence (obligation), and notes that specific possible propositions can overlap with necessities like temporal or spread propositions. For the more specific possible (akhaṣṣ), the same applies but the necessity is in some respect. The passage then generalizes: contradiction is reciprocal and modality consideration is uniform across affirmative/negative and universal/particular. The absolute and perpetual are contradictories, as are the general possible and necessary. This principle is self-evident ('this is clear').

Contradiction in Conditionals: Same Rules as Categoricals
Author states that contradiction in conditionals follows same rules as categoricals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that contradiction in conditional propositions follows the same conditions as categorical propositions.

Core Idea
Contradiction rules for conditionals mirror categoricals exactly.

This lesson examines the author's claim that the logical rules governing contradiction in conditional propositions (al-sharṭiyyāt) are identical to those for categoricals (al-ḥamliyyāt). Understanding this principle allows you to apply everything you already know about categorical contradiction to conditionals, saving effort and ensuring consistency. The passage opens a new chapter reinforcing this key unity.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening phrase
The author begins a new chapter (fasl) on contradiction in conditional propositions. Note the phrase 'its rule is the same as contradiction in categoricals'.
2
Identify the key equality claim
The author explicitly states that nothing differs among the things that must be considered in verification. This means all the same conditions—such as quality, quantity, and modality—apply equally to conditionals.
Conditionals include both muttasil and munfasil types.
3
Recall the conditions for categorical contradiction
From earlier lessons, categorical contradiction requires one universal affirmative and one particular negative (or vice versa) with the same subject and predicate, same tense, location, etc.
Review the previous section if needed.
4
Apply those conditions to conditionals
For a universal conditional like 'Every time A then B', its contradictory is 'Sometimes A and not B' (in muttasil). The same rules of quality and quantity hold: change the quality and quantity from universal to particular.
The same principle applies to munfasil conditionals.

All the considerations that apply to categorical contradiction—such as modality, quantity, and quality—apply equally to conditionals. Contradiction Patterns for Modal Categoricals
Author enumerates contradiction patterns for modal propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any modal categorical proposition based on its modality, quality, and quantity.

Core Idea
Contradiction in modal logic requires differing in quality, quantity, and modality.

In classical Islamic logic, contradicting a modal proposition is not merely flipping quality and quantity; the modality must also be transformed. This passage from al-Mantiq al-Kabir outlines the specific patterns: a non-perpetual proposition is contradicted by a perpetual proposition, a particular possible by a necessary proposition, and so on. Mastering these patterns is essential for constructing valid arguments and refutations in Islamic theology and jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the modal type
Determine if the proposition is non-perpetual (existential), particular possible, more specific possible, future possible, etc. This determines the required modal opposite.
The passage explicitly lists several types: 'al-wujūdiyya al-lā dā'ima', 'al-mumkina al-khāṣṣa', etc.
2
Determine opposite quality and quantity
The contradictory must differ in both quality (affirmative vs. negative) and quantity (universal vs. particular). For example, 'Every A is B' becomes 'Some A is not B'.
This is standard for all categoricals.
3
Determine the required modal opposite
For a non-perpetual proposition, the contradictory is perpetual with opposite quality. For a particular possible, the contradictory is necessary with opposite quality. For future possible, the same pattern applies.
The passage gives specific formulas: 'Every A is B not perpetually' is contradicted by 'Some A is not B perpetually' or 'Some A is B perpetually' depending on original quality.
4
Combine into the contradictory proposition
Combine the opposite quality, opposite quantity, and the required modality to form the correct contradictory. Verify that it has the same subject and predicate.
Check symmetry: if p contradicts q, then q contradicts p, as stated at the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة كيفا فيقال كل «أب» لا دائما بل ما دام وقت كذا؛ وذلك الوقت غير معين أيضًا، بعض «أ» ليس (ب) أصلا بالإطلاق العام أو بعضه «ب» دائمًا. وأما في الوجودية اللا دائمة فهو الدائمة المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفًا فيقال كل «أب» لا دائما ، بعض «أ» ليس «ب» دائمًا أو بعضه (ب) دائمًا. وأما في الممكنة الخاصة فهو الضرورية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الضرورية الموافقة كيفًا فيقال كل «أب» بالإمكان الخاص بعض (أ) ليس «أ» (((ب))) بالضرورة أو بعضه «ب» بالضرورة والضرورة فيه إما ضرورة العدم وهي الامتناع، وإما ضرورة الوجود وهي الوجوب في الحقيقة وإلا لا يصح، فإن الممكنة الخاصة قد تكون ضرورية نحو الوقتية والمنتشرة وأمثالهما. وأما في الأخص فكذلك لكن الضرورة فيها بوجه من الوجوه فيقال كل «أب» بالإمكان الأخص، بعض ( أ ) ليس «ب» بالضرورة أي ضرورة كانت أو بعضه «ب» بالضرورة كذلك. وعلى هذا في الإمكان الاستقبالي، فاعتبر بما عرفت فإن اعتبار الجهة في التناقض لا يختلف باختلاف القضايا الموجبة والسالبة والكلية والجزئية، والقضية لا تناقض قضية أخرى إلا وأن تكون تلك القضية تناقضها، فالمطلقة تناقض الدائمة فالدائمة إذن تناقض المطلقة. وكذا الممكنة العامة تناقض الضرورية، فالضرورية إذن تناقضها؛ إذ المنافاة بين القضيتين لا تكون مخصوصة بأحد الجانبين، وهذا ظاهر.
The universal opposite in quality and quantity or the perpetual opposite in quality, so it is said: 'Every A is B' not perpetually but as long as a certain time; and that time is also unspecified, 'Some A is not B at all' in the absolute sense, or 'Some A is B perpetually.' As for the existential non-perpetual, it is the perpetual opposite in quality and quantity or the perpetual agreeing in quality, so it is said: 'Every A is B' not perpetually, 'Some A is not B perpetually' or 'Some A is B perpetually.' As for the particular possible, it is the necessary opposite in quality and quantity or the necessary agreeing in quality, so it is said: 'Every A is B with particular possibility' 'Some A is not B necessarily' or 'Some A is B necessarily'; and the necessity here is either necessity of non-existence, i.e., impossibility, or necessity of existence, i.e., obligation in reality, otherwise it is not valid; for the particular possible may be necessary, like the temporal and distributive and their likes. As for the more specific, it is likewise, but the necessity therein is in some respect, so it is said: 'Every A is B with the more specific possibility' 'Some A is not B necessarily' i.e., any necessity, or 'Some A is B necessarily' likewise. And upon this is the future possibility; so consider what you have known; for the consideration of modality in contradiction does not differ with differences of affirmative and negative, universal and particular propositions; and a proposition does not contradict another proposition unless that proposition contradicts it; so the absolute contradicts the perpetual, so the perpetual therefore contradicts the absolute. Likewise the general possible contradicts the necessary, so the necessary therefore contradicts it; for the incompatibility between two propositions is not specific to one side, and this is evident.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage defines the patterns of contradiction for various modal categorical propositions. The author outlines how the contradictory of a proposition must differ in quality and quantity, and also in modality depending on the type. For non-perpetual propositions, the contradictory involves a perpetual proposition with opposite quality. For particular possible propositions, the contradictory is a necessary proposition. The author emphasizes that modality is essential in contradiction: the contradictory of a possible is necessary, and vice versa. The passage concludes with a general principle: contradiction is symmetric; if p contradicts q, then q contradicts p. The discussion covers specific cases like existential non-perpetual, particular possible, and future possibility, showing how each type maps to a specific contradictory form.

Contradiction in Conditional Propositions
Author applies rules of contradiction to conditional propositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contradictory of any conditional proposition by applying the rule of general possibility (al-imkān al-ʿāmm).

Core Idea
The contradictory of a necessary conditional is a general possible proposition with opposite quality.

Just as categorical propositions have contradictories governed by quantity and quality, conditional propositions have their own rules. In this passage, the author extends the logic of contradiction to conditionals, explaining how indefinite, absolute, and necessary conditionals are handled. The key is that the contradictory must differ in modality, and the general possible serves as the common contradictory for many types.

Guided Path
1
Classify the conditional type
Identify whether the conditional is indefinite (muhmala), absolute (muṭlaqa), or necessary (ḍarūriyya). For necessary conditionals, further distinguish absolutely necessary (ḍarūriyya muṭlaqa) from conditionally necessary (mashrūṭa).
The passage states that indefinite conditionals are like particulars in force.
2
Determine quantity and quality
Note the quantifier (universal or particular) and the affirmative/negative quality of the proposition. For example, 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C' is universal affirmative.
3
Find the general possible opposite
Contradiction requires a modality of general possibility (imkān ʿāmm) that is opposite in both quantity and quality. For a universal affirmative necessary conditional, the contradictory is particular negative with general possibility.
The passage says: 'What indicates the contradictory is the general possible opposite in quality and quantity.'
4
Construct the contradictory
Formulate the contradictory by prefixing 'Not necessarily' (laysa bi-l-ḍarūra) and appending 'with general possibility' (bi-l-imkān al-ʿāmm). For example, the contradictory of 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C' is 'Not necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C' with general possibility.
The author explicitly gives this example in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : [ في التناقض في الشرطيات ] وأما التناقض في الشرطيات فحكمه حكم التناقض في الحمليات فلا يختلف شيء ما من الأشياء التي يجب اعتبارها في التحقق سواء كانت الشرطيات من المهملات أو من غيرها، والغير من المطلقات أو الموجهات. أما المهملة فلا يناقضها من نوعها شيء لما أن الكليتين قد تكذبان في مادة الإمكان، والجزئيتين قد تصدقان كذلك، والمهملة في قوة الجزئية. فإنك إذا قلت: لو كان كذا لكان كذا فلا تدري أنه في جميع الأحوال أو في البعض منها. كما أن المهملة لا يناقضها من نوعها شيء فكذلك المطلقة لا يناقضها من نوعها شيء لاحتمال أن تكون كل واحدة منهما موجهة بجهة واحدة، وإن كانتا محصلتين في الكمية والكيفية، والاختلاف في الجهة من اللوازم كما مر . ولا يقال : إنما يكون كذلك أن لو كانت الجهة من اللوازم؛ إذ هي من اللوازم معنى، وإن لم يكن هي من اللوازم لفظا وهذا من جملة ما قد مرَّ الكلام فيه. ثم القضية الشرطية قد تكون مطلقة، وقد لا تكون بل تكون ضرورية مثلا؛ والضرورية قد تكون ضرورية مطلقة، وقد لا تكون بل تكون مشروطة مثلا . والضرورية المطلقة قد تكون من كليتين، وقد تكون من جزئيتين وقد تكون من مختلفتين كما مرّ من قبل ؛ وكذلك اللا مطلقة. وبالجملة فما يدل على النقيض في كل واحدة منهما هو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا كما هي بنفسها أو بصفة مرَّ ذكرها في المشروطتين. وقد مر من قبل أن رفع الضرورة إما بالضرورة وإما بالإمكان الخاص. والمشترك بينهما هو الإمكان العام فيقال في الضرورية المطلقة بالضرورة كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج»، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» بالإمكان العام، وفي غير المطلقة كما في المشروطة العامة هو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا كما يقال بالضرورة كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» ما دام «ب»، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» حين هو «ب» بالإمكان العام. وفي المشروطة الخاصة هو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا والدائمة الموافقة كيفا كما يقال بالضرورة
Chapter: On Contradiction in Conditionals. As for contradiction in conditionals, its rule is the same as contradiction in categoricals; nothing that should be considered in verification differs, whether the conditionals are indefinite or not, and the non-indefinite are absolute or modal. As for the indefinite, nothing of its own type contradicts it, because two universal propositions may both be false in a possible matter, and two particular propositions may both be true likewise, and the indefinite is like a particular. For if you say: 'If it were such, it would be such,' you do not know whether it is in all cases or in some of them. Just as the indefinite is not contradicted by anything of its own type, so too the absolute is not contradicted by anything of its own type, because it is possible that each of them is modal with one modality, even if they are determinate in quantity and quality, and difference in modality is among the necessary concomitants as previously mentioned. And it is not said: 'This would only be the case if modality were among the necessary concomitants'; indeed it is among the necessary concomitants in meaning, even if it is not among the necessary concomitants in wording, and this is part of what has been discussed. Then the conditional proposition may be absolute, or it may not be, but be necessary, for example. And the necessary may be absolutely necessary, or it may not be, but be conditional, for example. The absolutely necessary may consist of two universals, or two particulars, or two different types, as previously mentioned; similarly for the non-absolute. In summary, what indicates the contradictory in each of them is the general possible opposite in quality and quantity, either as it is itself or with a description that was mentioned in the two conditionals. It has been previously mentioned that the removal of necessity is either by necessity or by particular possibility. And the common factor between them is general possibility. So it is said regarding the absolutely necessary: 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C' and 'Not necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C' with general possibility. And regarding the non-absolute, as in the general conditional, it is the general possible temporal opposite in quality and quantity, as is said: 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C as long as B' and 'Not necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C when it is B' with general possibility. And regarding the particular conditional, it is the general possible temporal opposite in quality and quantity and the perpetual agreeing in quality, as is said: 'Necessarily'...
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage extends the rules of contradiction to conditional propositions. The author begins by stating that the same principles apply as for categoricals. He then addresses the indefinite conditional (muhmala): it is like a particular, so it cannot be contradicted by another indefinite because both could be true. Similarly, absolute conditionals cannot contradict each other because they may differ in modality. The author emphasizes that modality is a necessary concomitant in meaning even if not expressed. He then classifies conditionals into absolute, necessary, and subtypes. The contradictory of a necessary conditional is a general possible proposition with opposite quality and quantity. For the absolutely necessary, the contradictory is 'not necessarily' with general possibility. For conditionals with temporal restrictions (mashrūṭa), the contradictory involves a temporal general possible. The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but the pattern is clear: the contradictory of a conditional must differ in modality, and the general possible serves as the common contradictory for many types.

المشروطة
الإمكان العام

The contradictory of a conditional proposition always requires a shift in modality, with general possibility serving as the universal contradictory for necessary conditionals.

Why Indefinite and Absolute Conditionals Have No Same-Type Contradictory
Author explains why indefinite and absolute conditionals lack a contradictory of their own type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why indefinite (muhmala) and absolute (mutlaqa) conditional propositions lack a contradictory of their own type.

Core Idea
Indefinite conditionals are like particulars; absolute conditionals hide modal differences — both lack same-type contradictories.

You already know that contradictory propositions must differ in truth value in every possible case. But what happens when a conditional does not specify its scope (indefinite) or its modality (absolute)? In this lesson, you will see why such conditionals cannot have a direct contradictory of the same type, based on the logical principles established earlier.

Guided Path
1
Classify the conditional types
The passage groups conditionals into indefinite (muhmala) and non-indefinite, then the latter into absolute (mutlaqa) and modal. Identify each type in the text.
Recall that indefinite means without quantifier; absolute means without modal specification.
2
Understand why indefinite conditionals = particulars
The author says 'al-muhmala fi quwwat al-juz'iyya' — indefinite conditionals function like particular categoricals. Check the example: 'If such-and-such, then such-and-such' does not tell you if it holds always or sometimes.
Just as particular propositions have no contradictory of the same type (since both particulars can be true in possibility), indefinite conditionals also lack a same-type contradictory.
3
See why absolute conditionals also lack a contradictory
Two absolute conditionals that are opposite in quantity and quality (e.g., one universal affirmative, one particular negative) may still both be false or both true if they differ in modality — one might be necessary, the other possible.
The difference in modality is a 'lazim' (concomitant) in meaning, even if not stated in wording, and this prevents them from being true contradictories.
4
Connect to the principle of modal concomitance
The author refers to earlier discussion: modality is a concomitant in meaning. This means that when evaluating contradiction, you must consider the implicit modality, which breaks the neat opposition of simple conditionals.
Thus, no conditional of the same surface type (indefinite or absolute) can serve as the contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرطيات من المهملات أو من غيرها، والغير من المطلقات أو الموجهات. أما المهملة فلا يناقضها من نوعها شيء لما أن الكليتين قد تكذبان في مادة الإمكان، والجزئيتين قد تصدقان كذلك، والمهملة في قوة الجزئية. فإنك إذا قلت: لو كان كذا لكان كذا فلا تدري أنه في جميع الأحوال أو في البعض منها. كما أن المهملة لا يناقضها من نوعها شيء فكذلك المطلقة لا يناقضها من نوعها شيء لاحتمال أن تكون كل واحدة منهما موجهة بجهة واحدة، وإن كانتا محصلتين في الكمية والكيفية، والاختلاف في الجهة من اللوازم كما مر. ولا يقال: إنما يكون كذلك أن لو كانت الجهة من اللوازم؛ إذ هي من اللوازم معنى، وإن لم يكن هي من اللوازم لفظا وهذا من جملة ما قد مرَّ الكلام فيه.
Conditional propositions are either indefinite or not, and the latter are either absolute or modal. As for the indefinite, nothing of its type contradicts it because both universals may be false in the matter of possibility, and both particulars may be true likewise, and the indefinite is in the force of the particular. For if you say: 'If such-and-such were the case, then such-and-such would be the case,' you do not know whether it is in all cases or in some of them. Just as the indefinite has no contradictory of its type, so too the absolute has no contradictory of its type because it is possible that each of them is modal with one modality, even if they are determinate in quantity and quality, and the difference in modality is among the concomitants, as previously mentioned. And it is not said: 'It would only be so if modality were among the concomitants in wording'; for it is among the concomitants in meaning, even if it is not among the concomitants in wording, and this is part of what has been discussed.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage discusses the contradiction of indefinite and absolute conditional propositions. The author explains that indefinite conditionals (al-muhmala) have no contradictory of their own type because they are logically equivalent to particular propositions. In conditional logic, just as in categorical logic, an indefinite proposition behaves like a particular ('المهملة في قوة الجزئية'). For example, if someone says 'If this occurs, then that occurs,' without specifying whether it is always or sometimes, it is like a particular and thus has no direct contradictory among indefinite propositions. Similarly, absolute conditionals (al-mutlaqa) also lack a contradictory of their own type because two opposite absolute conditionals may differ in modality (e.g., one is necessary, the other possible) even if their quantities and qualities match. This difference in modality is a 'lazim' (concomitant) in meaning, though not necessarily in wording, so it prevents a straightforward contradiction. The author emphasizes that this understanding comes from the principles established earlier.

Key Terms
المهملة
المطلقة
النقيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because they may differ in modality even if they match in quantity and quality
C) Because they are always true
D) Because they cannot be expressed in Arabic

Key Takeaway
Indefinite and absolute conditionals lack a contradictory of their own type because the former functions as a particular and the latter may involve modal differences that prevent direct opposition.

Contradiction of Necessary Absolute Conditionals
Author defines the contradiction for absolute and necessary absolute conditionals using general possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the contradictory of an absolutely necessary conditional proposition using general possibility.

Core Idea
Negating a necessary conditional yields a general possibility, not a simple denial.

In this passage, the author explains the precise form of the contradictory for necessary conditionals. Understanding this is crucial for correctly negating conditional claims in logical arguments, especially in Islamic theology and jurisprudence where conditional necessity is debated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of conditional
Determine whether the conditional is absolute (mutlaqa) or necessary (daruriyya). The text focuses on necessary absolute conditionals, e.g., 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C.'
2
Recall the rule for removal of necessity
The removal of necessity (raf' al-darura) can be done either by asserting the opposite necessity or by using special possibility (imkan khas). Both share general possibility (imkan 'amm) as common ground.
3
Form the contradictory
To contradict a necessary conditional like 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C', the contradictory is 'Not (necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C)' — expressed as 'by general possibility', meaning it is possible that A is B and C is not the case.
The contradictory differs in quantity and quality from the original.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
For instance, the conditional 'Necessarily, if a hadith is mutawatir, it entails certain knowledge' has the contradictory 'It is possible that a hadith is mutawatir and does not entail certain knowledge' (logical possibility, not factual claim).
This illustrates the logical form outside abstract terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القضية الشرطية قد تكون مطلقة، وقد لا تكون بل تكون ضرورية مثلا؛ والضرورية قد تكون ضرورية مطلقة، وقد لا تكون بل تكون مشروطة مثلا. والضرورية المطلقة قد تكون من كليتين، وقد تكون من جزئيتين وقد تكون من مختلفتين كما مرّ من قبل؛ وكذلك اللا مطلقة. وبالجملة فما يدل على النقيض في كل واحدة منهما هو الممكنة العامة المخالفة كما وكيفا كما هي بنفسها أو بصفة مرَّ ذكرها في المشروطتين. وقد مر من قبل أن رفع الضرورة إما بالضرورة وإما بالإمكان الخاص. والمشترك بينهما هو الإمكان العام فيقال في الضرورة المطلقة بالضرورة كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج»، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» بالإمكان العام.
Then the conditional proposition may be absolute, or it may not be, but rather necessary, for example; and the necessary may be absolutely necessary, or it may not be, but rather conditioned, for example. The absolutely necessary may be from two universals, or from two particulars, or from two different ones, as passed earlier; and likewise the non-absolute. In summary, what indicates the contradictory in each of them is the general possibility differing in quantity and quality, as it is by itself or by a quality mentioned in the two conditioned propositions. It has passed earlier that the removal of necessity is either by necessity or by special possibility. The commonality between them is general possibility, so it is said in the absolutely necessary: 'necessarily whenever A is B, it is C' – it is not that 'whenever A is B, it is C' by general possibility.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage builds on the previous discussion by addressing absolute and necessary conditional propositions. The author explains that a conditional can be absolute (mutlaqa) or necessary (daruriyya), and the necessary can be absolutely necessary (daruriyya mutlaqa) or conditioned (mashruta). The absolutely necessary conditional, regardless of whether its components are universal or particular, has a contradictory that is a 'mumkina 'amma' (general possibility) differing in quantity and quality. The removal of necessity (رفع الضرورة) can be achieved either by asserting the opposite necessity (i.e., the contradictory's necessity) or by using 'imkan khas' (special possibility). However, the shared element between these two methods is 'imkan 'amm' (general possibility). Thus, for the proposition 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C', its contradictory is 'Not (necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C) by general possibility', meaning it is possible that A is B and C does not hold. This shows the standard form for negating necessary conditionals.

Key Terms
ضرورية مطلقة
الممكنة العامة
رفع الضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Not: whenever A is B, it is C, by general possibility
C) Possibly, whenever A is B, it is C (with possibility of the whole conditional)
D) Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is not C (by special possibility)

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a necessary absolute conditional is a general possibility proposition that denies the necessity, not the conditional itself.

Contradictions of Conditioned Conditionals (Mashruta: General and Special)
Author lists contradictions for conditioned conditionals from both sides.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to correctly formulate the contradictory of a general or special conditioned conditional proposition from either the antecedent or consequent side.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a conditioned conditional is a temporal possibility, not a simple negation.

In Islamic logic, conditional propositions often carry temporal conditions. This lesson teaches how to contradict such propositions accurately, a skill essential for constructing valid arguments in kalam and usul al-fiqh. The passage distinguishes between general and special conditioned conditionals and provides precise formulations for their contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of conditioned conditional
Determine if it is general (mashruta 'amma) or special (mashruta khassa). The general conditional holds with necessity whenever the condition holds; the special holds only for the duration of the condition.
General: 'as long as B' implies necessity throughout. Special: 'not perpetually but as long as B' implies only temporary necessity.
2
Locate the side of the condition
Is the condition on the antecedent (e.g., 'as long as B') or on the consequent ('as long as C')? The side determines which term is temporally qualified.
The antecedent side: 'whenever A is B, it is C as long as B'. The consequent side: 'whenever A is B, it is C as long as C'.
3
For general conditioned: contradictory is a general temporal possibility
The contradictory differs in quantity and quality: it negates the conditional while the condition holds, and asserts it is possible that it is not the case. Example: 'Not: whenever A is B, it is C while it is B, by general possibility'.
The original is necessary; the contradictory is possible. The condition (while it is B) is preserved in the negation.
4
For special conditioned: contradictory offers two options
Either the same general temporal possibility as above, or a perpetual proposition (da'ima) that agrees in quality. The perpetual option says: 'It may be that whenever A is B, it is C perpetually'.
The special conditional is not perpetual; its contradictory can be a perpetual positive or a temporal possibility.
5
Write the contradictory proposition
Using the pattern: 'Not: whenever A is B, it is C while it is B, by general possibility' (for general) and for special, add 'or it may be that whenever A is B, it is C perpetually'.
Ensure the condition matches the side: use 'while it is B' for antecedent side, 'while it is C' for consequent side.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي غير المطلقة كما في المشروطة العامة هو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا كما يقال بالضرورة كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» ما دام «ب»، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» حين هو «ب» بالإمكان العام. وفي المشروطة الخاصة هو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا والدائمة الموافقة كيفا كما يقال بالضرورة كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» لا دائما بل ما دام «ب»، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» كان ج حين هو «ب» بالإمكان العام، أو قد يكون إذا كان «أب» كان «ج» دائما. وأما في المشروطة العامة من جانب التالي فهو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا كما يقال بالضرورة كلما كان «أب» كان «ج» ما دام «ج»، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» كان (ج) حين هو «ج» بالإمكان العام. وفي المشروطة الخاصة من جانب التالي فكذلك هو الممكنة العامة الحينية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفا كما يقال بالضرورة كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» لا دائما بل ما دام (ج)، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» كان «ج» حين هو (ج) بالإمكان العام أو قد يكون إذا كان «أب» كان «ج» دائما.
And in the non-absolute, such as the general conditioned, it is the general temporal possibility differing in quantity and quality, as is said: 'necessarily whenever A is B, it is C as long as B'; it is not that 'whenever A is B, it is C while it is B' by general possibility. And in the special conditioned, it is the general temporal possibility differing in quantity and quality, and the perpetual agreeing in quality, as is said: 'necessarily whenever A is B, it is C not perpetually but as long as B'; it is not that 'whenever A is B, it is C while it is B' by general possibility, or it may be that 'whenever A is B, it is C perpetually.' As for the general conditioned from the side of the consequent, it is the general temporal possibility differing in quantity and quality, as is said: 'necessarily whenever A is B, it is C as long as C'; it is not that 'whenever A is B, it is C while it is C' by general possibility. And in the special conditioned from the side of the consequent, likewise it is the general temporal possibility differing in quantity and quality, or the perpetual agreeing in quality, as is said: 'necessarily whenever A is B, it is C not perpetually but as long as C'; it is not that 'whenever A is B, it is C while it is C' by general possibility, or it may be that 'whenever A is B, it is C perpetually.'
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage details the contradictions for conditioned conditional propositions from both the antecedent and consequent sides. The author distinguishes between general conditioned (mashruta 'amma) and special conditioned (mashruta khassa). For the general conditioned from the side of the antecedent (i.e., the condition is on the antecedent), such as 'Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C as long as B', its contradictory is a general temporal possibility (mumkina 'amma hiniyya) that differs in quantity and quality: 'Not: whenever A is B, it is C while it is B, by general possibility'. For the special conditioned from the side of the antecedent (where the conditional is not perpetual but only holds as long as the condition lasts), the contradictory is either the same general temporal possibility or a perpetual (da'ima) proposition that agrees in quality, as in: either 'Not: whenever A is B, it is C while it is B' or 'It may be that whenever A is B, it is C perpetually.' Similarly, for the general conditioned from the side of the consequent (where the condition is on the consequent, e.g., 'as long as C'), the contradictory follows the same pattern but with the condition on C. The author provides examples using the letters A, B, C. This systematic enumeration shows the care needed in modal logic for conditional propositions.

Key Terms
المشروطة العامة
المشروطة الخاصة
الممكنة العامة الحينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is not C as long as B
B) Not: whenever A is B, it is C while it is B, by general possibility
C) Possibly, whenever A is B, it is C as long as B
D) Necessarily, whenever A is B, it is C perpetually

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a conditioned conditional is always a temporal possibility, with the special conditioned allowing an additional perpetual alternative.

?

Contradiction of the General Time-Conditioned Conditional (al-Waqtiyya al-'Amma)
Author defines contradictory for general time-conditioned conditional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the contradictory of a general time-conditioned conditional in both its universal affirmative form and its contradictory possibility form.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a necessary universal conditional at a time is a possible particular negation.

General time-conditioned conditionals (al-waqtiyya al-'amma) are universal and necessary for a specific time. Their contradictory must differ in both quantity and quality, resulting in a general time-qualified possibility proposition. Understanding this relationship is essential for evaluating modal claims in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original proposition
The general time-conditioned conditional has the form: 'Necessarily, whenever A is B at time T, it is C.' This is a universal affirmative necessary proposition restricted to a specific time.
The time T is fixed, not a duration.
2
Determine the contradictory's modality and quantity
The contradictory must be a possibility proposition (not necessity) and must be particular (not universal). So it becomes 'It is not the case that whenever A is B at time T, it is C, by general possibility.'
The phrase 'by general possibility' indicates the modality is possibility, not necessity.
3
Express the contradictory in Arabic form
Using the source: 'ليس كلما كان «أب» وقت كذا كان (ج) بالإمكان العام.' Note the change from 'بالضرورة' to 'بالإمكان العام' and the addition of negation 'ليس'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في الوقتية العامة فهو الممكنة العامة الوقتية المخالفة كما وكيفا كما يقال بالضرورة كلما كان «أب» وقت كذا كان «ج»، ليس كلَّما كان «أب» وقت كذا كان (ج) بالإمكان العام. وفي الوقتية الخاصة هو الممكنة العامة الوقتية المخالفة كما وكيفا أو الدائمة الموافقة كيفا كما يقال بالضرورة كلما كان «أب» وقت كذا كان «ج» لا دائما بل وقت كذا، ليس كلما كان «أب» وقت كذا كان دائما بالإمكان العام أو قد يكون إذا كان «أب» كان «ج» دائما.

Commentary
This passage covers time-conditioned (waqtiyya) conditionals, which specify a particular time (e.g., 'at time T'). For the general time-conditioned (waqtiyya 'amma), the conditional 'Necessarily, whenever A is B at time T, it is C' has a contradictory that is a general time-qualified possibility (mumkina 'amma waqtiyya) differing in quantity and quality: 'Not: whenever A is B at time T, it is C' by general possibility. For the special time-conditioned (waqtiyya khassa), where the conditional is not perpetual but only holds at that specific time, the contradictory is either the same general time-qualified possibility or a perpetual proposition that agrees in quality. For example, for 'Necessarily, whenever A is B at time T, it is C, not perpetually but at time T,' the contradictory is either 'Not: whenever A is B at time T, it is perpetual' by general possibility, or 'It may be that whenever A is B, it is C perpetually.' This shows the pattern: special time-conditioned adds the option of a perpetual contradictory.

Contradiction of the Special Time-Conditioned Conditional (al-Waqtiyya al-Khassa)
Author defines contradictory for special time-conditioned conditional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two possible contradictories of a special time-conditioned conditional.

Core Idea
The special waqtiyya has two contradictories: a possibility proposition or a perpetual proposition agreeing in quality.

Special time-conditioned conditionals (al-waqtiyya al-khassa) are not perpetual but hold only at a designated time. Their contradictory offers two options: either a general time-qualified possibility differing in quantity and quality, or a perpetual proposition that agrees in quality. This dual possibility reflects the non-perpetual nature of the original.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original proposition
The special time-conditioned conditional has the form: 'Necessarily, whenever A is B at time T, it is C, not perpetually but at time T.' Note the stipulation 'not perpetually' makes it specific to that time.
This distinguishes it from the general type which does not explicitly negate perpetuity.
2
Extract the first contradictory option
The first contradictory is a general time-qualified possibility that differs in quantity and quality: 'Not: whenever A is B at time T, it is perpetual, by general possibility.' This negates the 'perpetual' claim.
3
Extract the second contradictory option
The second contradictory agrees in quality (affirmative) but changes modality to possibility and removes the time restriction: 'It may be that whenever A is B, it is C perpetually.' This is a perpetual possibility proposition.
This option is unique to the special waqtiyya, not found in the general type.

Contradictories of Existential Conditionals
Definition of contradictories for existential conditionals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the contradictory of a general existential conditional in Islamic modal logic using the rules of quantity and quality change.

Core Idea
The contradictory of 'sometimes' is 'never' under possibility, not necessity.

In Islamic logic, existential conditionals assert that a conditional holds at some time, not always. Their contradictory is a general possibility proposition that denies the conditional holds at any time. This distinction is crucial for constructing valid arguments in fields like Kalam and Usul al-Fiqh, where temporal modalities affect the meaning of proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of existential conditional
Read the conditional: if it says 'whenever A is B, it is C at some time', it is a general existential (muntasheera 'amma). If it says 'not perpetually but at some times', it is a special existential (mashruta khassa). Note the modal qualifier (necessity vs possibility).
The general existential is equivalent to 'sometimes A is B then C'.
2
Formulate the contradictory according to the rule
The contradictory of a general existential conditional is a general possibility proposition that differs in quantity and quality. Quantitatively, change 'whenever' to 'not whenever'; qualitatively, change affirmative to negative. Apply the modal from the original: if the original is necessary, the contradictory is possible.
The text gives the example: 'Not: whenever A is B, it is C at all' by general possibility.
3
Test with an Islamic example
Take a conditional from Islamic jurisprudence: 'Whenever someone drinks intoxicants, they are sinful' (perpetual). But as an existential: 'Whenever someone drinks intoxicants, they are sometimes (not always) sinful' is false. Its contradictory: 'Not whenever someone drinks intoxicants, they are sinful at all, by possibility' (i.e., it is not necessarily that every instance of drinking intoxicants results in sin, because of exceptions?). Ensure the modal matches.
This illustrates how modal restrictions affect rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

As for the general existential, it is the general possibility differing in quantity and quality, as is said: 'necessarily whenever A is B, it is C at some time'; it is not that 'whenever A is B, it is C at all' by general possibility. And in the special conditioned [but likely existential], it is the general possibility differing in quantity and quality, or the perpetual agreeing in quality, as is said: 'necessarily whenever A is B, it is C not perpetually but at some times'; it is not that 'whenever A is B, it is C at all' by general possibility, or it may be that 'whenever A is B, it is C perpetually.' As for the non-necessary existential, it is the perpetual differing in quantity and quality, or the necessity...
